  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_83834772-7c34-41b4-9875-c32b23f18ef9'

<span id="freeTextContainer6297348436615565267">Jamaica in 1665 is a rough outpost of the English crown, a minor colony holding out against the vast supremacy of the Spanish empire. Port Royal, Jamaica′s capital, a cut-throat town of taverns, grog shops, and bawdy houses, is devoid of London′s luxuries; life here can end swiftly with dysentery or a dagger in your back. But for Captain Charles Hunter it is a life that ca</span>
  <span id="freeText6297348436615565267" style="display:none">Jamaica in 1665 is a rough outpost of the English crown, a minor colony holding out against the vast supremacy of the Spanish empire. Port Royal, Jamaica′s capital, a cut-throat town of taverns, grog shops, and bawdy houses, is devoid of London′s luxuries; life here can end swiftly with dysentery or a dagger in your back. But for Captain Charles Hunter it is a life that can also lead to riches, if he abides by the island′s code. In the name of His Majesty King Charles II of England, gold in Spanish hands is gold for the taking. And law in the New World is made by those who take it into their hands.<br /><br />Word in port is that the Spanish treasure galleon El Trinidad, fresh from New Spain, is stalled in nearby Matanceros harbor awaiting repairs. Heavily fortified, the impregnable Spanish outpost is guarded by the blood-swiller Cazalla, a favorite commander of King Philip IV himself. With the governor′s backing, Hunter assembles a roughneck crew to infiltrate the enemy island and commandeer the galleon, along with its fortune in Spanish gold. The raid is as perilous as the bloody legends of Matanceros suggest, and Hunter will lose more than one man before he finds himself on the island′s shores, where dense jungle and the firepower of Spanish infantry are all that stand between him and the treasure.<br /><br />With the help of his cunning crew, Hunter hijacks El Trinidad and escapes the deadly clutches of Cazalla, leaving plenty of carnage in his wake. But his troubles have just begun. . . .</span>
  <a data-text-id="6297348436615565267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/872547117?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153333-pirate-latitudes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872547117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10424116030501444498">I have seen many reviews critical of this book, but I thought it was a great adventure with interesting characters and twists. Perhaps people are critical of the fact that this is unlike Crichton's other titles, but much like Eaters of the Dead and The Great Train Robbery; it is great, well researched historical fiction. (Note: between Latitudes, Eaters, and Train Robbery, I liked this one the best)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82295123" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82295123" />
    <a title="murph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169440-murph"><img alt="murph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1211995530p2/1169440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82295123?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="murph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="murph" href="/user/show/1169440-murph">murph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82295123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer600475171950958401"><em>"If only I'd have encrypted my hard drive...."</em><br/><br/><br/>You have to think Michael Crichton's ghost is mouthing those words.<br/><br/>Written in 2006 and published only after being digitally pried from the late author's cold, dead computer - Pirate Latitudes comes across as a vanity project never intended to see the light of day. <br/><br/>I'm sure it was great fun to write, but Crichton's attempt to inject research into worn out pirate clichés falls far short of a good story. Several parts of the story read as if they were f</span>
  <span id="freeText600475171950958401" style="display:none"><em>"If only I'd have encrypted my hard drive...."</em><br /><br /><br />You have to think Michael Crichton's ghost is mouthing those words.<br /><br />Written in 2006 and published only after being digitally pried from the late author's cold, dead computer - Pirate Latitudes comes across as a vanity project never intended to see the light of day. <br /><br />I'm sure it was great fun to write, but Crichton's attempt to inject research into worn out pirate clichés falls far short of a good story. Several parts of the story read as if they were first drafts - the prefunctory description of the sword battle between the hero and his nemesis - or the bland recitation of Cpt. Hunter collecting on his debts near the finale. <br /><br />A lot is thrown into the mix: Privateers! Galleons! Cannibals! Saucy wenches! Even a pointless encounter with a sea monster! But forcing your readers to eat everything on the pirate buffet doesn't make for a good meal. I suspect Mr. Crichton knew this book was due for a major rewrite - but his publishers knew the Crichton name would only sell for a short time longer. <br /><br />Pity. I was hungry for a good pirate yarn. This wasn't it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="600475171950958401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298960424" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8420010850344100389">Pirates! Huzzah! What could possibly ruin a rollicking, randy, riotous pirate adventure?...Plenty. <br/><br/>Crichton died before this was published and in all likelihood he wasn't finished with it. I would like to think that if he'd lived he would have worked on this more, rounded out the characters, twisted up the plot a bit, and run it through the edit mill a few times before handing it off to the publisher. I mean there are some passages towards the end that are on the very edge of not making any sens</span>
  <span id="freeText8420010850344100389" style="display:none">Pirates! Huzzah! What could possibly ruin a rollicking, randy, riotous pirate adventure?...Plenty. <br /><br />Crichton died before this was published and in all likelihood he wasn't finished with it. I would like to think that if he'd lived he would have worked on this more, rounded out the characters, twisted up the plot a bit, and run it through the edit mill a few times before handing it off to the publisher. I mean there are some passages towards the end that are on the very edge of not making any sense. <br /><br />I picked this book up on a lark, having never read Crichton before, but having a love of pirate adventures. The adventure part was alright. It's how the two star rating was obtained. However, this probably shouldn't have seen the light of day.</span>

<div id="review_2131570465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2131570465" />
    <a title="P. Lundburg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60599035-p-lundburg"><img alt="P. Lundburg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506383035p2/60599035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2131570465?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P. Lundburg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="P. Lundburg" href="/user/show/60599035-p-lundburg">P. Lundburg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60599035-p-lundburg?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60599035-p-lundburg?shelf=nature-literature">nature-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60599035-p-lundburg?shelf=well-known-authors">well-known-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2131570465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3179263875729792509">Scanning the reviews of this fantastic pirate novel, I'm a bit stunned at how many low ratings there are. Two important things for those reviewers to bear in mind: 1) this is way outside Crichton's normal 'genre,' and so readers will look askance at this venture into uncharted waters (couldn't resist the pun!), and 2) the book was found on Crichton's computer after he died, so it may well be that he wasn't finished with it.<br/><br/>On that last point, I agree with some reviewers that the book lapses into</span>
  <span id="freeText3179263875729792509" style="display:none">Scanning the reviews of this fantastic pirate novel, I'm a bit stunned at how many low ratings there are. Two important things for those reviewers to bear in mind: 1) this is way outside Crichton's normal 'genre,' and so readers will look askance at this venture into uncharted waters (couldn't resist the pun!), and 2) the book was found on Crichton's computer after he died, so it may well be that he wasn't finished with it.<br /><br />On that last point, I agree with some reviewers that the book lapses into being slow in places. Again, perhaps these were sections Crichton intended to revise (and let's not forget that the book would never have made it to print without the publisher's editors getting a go-round at it... yes, they have now that it was found and published, but not with the benefit of the back-and-forth that happens between authors and editors), but even so, I think even the slow sections contribute to the story. Characterization is very difficult to do in the midst of action, so most writers do most of that in what could be called "slow sections" of a book. Nonetheless, it is fair to level criticism at these slow parts.<br /><br />In terms of the story itself, it's a fantastic story about a Spanish, gold-bearing ship in the 1660s that is holed up in a garrisoned Spanish island port. The protagonist commandeers the vessel and a new set of fast-moving adventure segments begins. Not that the bulk of the book was void of adventure prior to that--it wasn't. I love the characterization Crichton builds, and that is the one part of this story that I would say DOES fit with standard Crichton: the way he builds his characters with attention to their history as well as (without being too overt about it) their psyche.<br /><br />On the whole, this is a great book. For pirate story lovers, this is a must-read. For Crichton fans, it is a must-read. For the average reader . . . well, you can do a lot worse, I can assure you of that.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3179263875729792509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_485853820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/485853820" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/485853820?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Noir and pirate-fiction fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer485853820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8525945572679598815">Since I greatly enjoyed Crichton's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7669.Timeline' title='Timeline by Michael Crichton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Timeline</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park' title='Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jurassic Park</a> (though I have yet to review the latter), I hoped to find a work of similar quality in this posthumous novel, though I knew that its ratings here on Goodreads varied widely. As usual, my reaction is my own; and as is sometimes the case, it falls somewhere between the extremes.<br/><br/>Crichton, of course, was best known for his science fiction. Here, he branches out into historical fiction, in a tale that doesn't really have any SF elements at</span>
  <span id="freeText8525945572679598815" style="display:none">Since I greatly enjoyed Crichton's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7669.Timeline" title="Timeline by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Timeline</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park" title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Jurassic Park</a> (though I have yet to review the latter), I hoped to find a work of similar quality in this posthumous novel, though I knew that its ratings here on Goodreads varied widely. As usual, my reaction is my own; and as is sometimes the case, it falls somewhere between the extremes.<br /><br />Crichton, of course, was best known for his science fiction. Here, he branches out into historical fiction, in a tale that doesn't really have any SF elements at all. (Some readers might assume that the references to a "kraken" are an exception to this; but the description makes it clear that the creature envisioned is actually a giant squid, a marine animal that really does exist, and is thought to be the source of a good deal of pre-modern "sea monster" lore.) But his time-travel novel <i>Timeline</i> also has a mostly historical setting, and (though I haven't read it myself) his <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7673.Eaters_of_the_Dead" title="Eaters of the Dead by Michael Crichton" rel="nofollow noopener">Eaters of the Dead</a>, despite having an SF element, is also set in a historical milieu. So this isn't a total departure from the rest of his work; and it exhibits the same obvious concern for meticulously detailed factual research, and the same zest for gripping, high-intensity action that's evident in the other Crichton works I've read. In those respects, it doesn't disappoint. Some reviewers complain that protagonist Capt. Hunter faces too many varied and successive dangerous challenges for the plot to be "realistic." But we're dealing here with an action novel; jeopardy and derring-do is what it's about, and from that perspective, it isn't a defect that it has a lot of it. The characterizations are vivid, and the 17th-century Caribbean setting is very well realized.<br /><br />Obviously, this is pirate fiction (a sub-genre of historical fiction I haven't read much else of, except for <i>Treasure Island</i>, though I have a few other pirate novels on my to-read shelf). So by definition, this is focused on characters who attack and forcibly plunder other people's ships. To be sure, Charles Hunter and others of his ilk are particular about drawing a distinction between themselves and "pirates" --if you call them that, you may get challenged to a duel! They stress the fact that they're "privateers;" they don't prey on the ships of their fellow Englishmen, only on those of the national enemy, the Spanish. (To be sure, in 1665, England and Spain are nominally at "peace," which creates interesting legal difficulties for privateers; but in practice, in the Caribbean the agents of both countries prey on each other's shipping with as much abandon as they would in a declared war.) To be fair, privateer captains and crews might think of themselves as fighting the enemy in a war, not as seagoing outlaws. And even novels dealing directly with pirates as such aren't necessarily morally nihilistic; light shines most clearly against darkness, so dark moral environments often serve to bring out the goodness of decent characters who inhabit them.<br /><br />For me, though, the main problem here is that light is largely nonexistent in the darkness that Crichton creates. Like Stevenson, he definitely does NOT romanticize piracy; on the contrary, he depicts both the physical and moral grunginess of the "Pirate Latitudes" with a remorseless realism that isn't necessarily a bad thing. But unlike Stevenson's cast of characters, <i>none</i> of those introduced here are really very likeable; self-interest, greed, and lust are pretty much everybody's main motivations for behavior, from the governor of Jamaica on down to his lowly serving maid, and much respect for human life would be as uncommon an attitude as genuine belief in Santa Claus. We're very much in the same uniformly dark and morally pessimistic landscape of classical noir; Port Royal has more in common with Sam Spade's San Francisco than the passing of nearly three centuries would make you think. Yes, Hunter thinks he has a certain "honor," some characters are far more evil than others (the psychopath Cazalla being the worst), and some have legitimate grievances and tragic formative circumstances that we can sympathize with. We can root for Hunter and his crew, given their opponents' villainy, and even give some of them a degree of respect. But in general, this isn't a novel that has a very positive "moral tendency," or an optimistic or positive message. That differs from the other Crichton novels I've read, which have a real moral vision. An added criticism would be that all females here, from professional prostitutes to married upper-class socialites, are pictured as sexually promiscuous and insatiable. This isn't "realism," any more than an imaginary universe where nobody's genuinely good is realistic; rather, it's pretty much a fantasy concocted by males (of whatever age) who are mature enough physically to have sexual desire, but not mature enough psychologically to control it responsibly. Finally, there are also several places where sloppy editing is evident, or cases where characters know or do something that Crichton wants them to for plot purposes, but realistically wouldn't, IMO. (And while a person can hide underwater for a long time by breathing through a hollow reed placed in the mouth, he/she would first have to be in a place where there would actually be access to a reed.)<br /><br />Bad language here isn't any worse or more abundant than you'd expect, given the type of milieu these people inhabit; and while there's a fair amount of sex, it isn't explicit. Violence here is pervasive, though, and frequently pretty graphic; if this were a movie (and it's reportedly been optioned for one), it would definitely be rated R on that account.<br /><br />A final note: despite the realistic-sounding details of the short Epilogue, that explains what eventually happened to the various surviving characters, none of the Epilogue is factual. Hunter and all of the other characters are fictional creations, and the plot isn't directly based on any real events.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8525945572679598815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_80332059" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80332059" />
    <a title="Kandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice"><img alt="Kandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231810788p2/1396160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80332059?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kandice" href="/user/show/1396160-kandice">Kandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80332059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15167546638581530195">I was so happy to hear they were publishing this book. Crichton's death was so sudden and unexpected I literally mourned the untold stories we lost with his passing.<br/><br/>Told as something of a more "realistic", less "Disney" Pirates of the Carribean, Crichton weaves the tale of Captain Charles Hunter's greatest raid of a Spanish treasure ship. From the first chapter, we are placed in the adventure and it ends up being a quick, fun ride.<br/><br/>The story was pure Chrichton, well told, detailed, obviously well</span>
  <span id="freeText15167546638581530195" style="display:none">I was so happy to hear they were publishing this book. Crichton's death was so sudden and unexpected I literally mourned the untold stories we lost with his passing.<br /><br />Told as something of a more "realistic", less "Disney" Pirates of the Carribean, Crichton weaves the tale of Captain Charles Hunter's greatest raid of a Spanish treasure ship. From the first chapter, we are placed in the adventure and it ends up being a quick, fun ride.<br /><br />The story was pure Chrichton, well told, detailed, obviously well researched, but the beginning left something to be desired. Usually with his books I can quickly choose a character to root for as well as one to hate. The plot of this book didn't suffer, but the little character quirks and ticks I've come to love him for were missing. I hope this was because he wasn't quite finished. <br /><br />I've never written a novel, so don't know if this is possible, but the "Crichton character magic" showed up from page 187, chapter 27, Monkey Bay. The entire flavor became richer, more detailed, exciting. Is it possible he had already fine tuned the second half of the book and was planning on doing the same to the first half? It seemed that way.<br /><br />Had he lived, I bet this could have been a five star book. The story itslef was worthy of it now, but the lack in the first half was worth a star less for me. I will miss him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15167546638581530195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8249384835155853372">Welcome to the good ship Cassandra! She will take you on exhilarating adventure on the high seas of the Carribean, looking for unknown treasures on a Spanish war ship. You will meet her Captain and come to know his ways and why he finds himself surrounded by a crew of unforgetable characters that you are going to love getting to know. And know them you will.   <span id="freeText8249384835155853372" style="display:none">Welcome to the good ship Cassandra! She will take you on exhilarating adventure on the high seas of the Carribean, looking for unknown treasures on a Spanish war ship. You will meet her Captain and come to know his ways and why he finds himself surrounded by a crew of unforgetable characters that you are going to love getting to know. And know them you will. This is great stuff that just keeps happening page after page.<br /> I guess in the end, it is what is missing from this story that I just cannot stop thinking about. Port Royal and all it's people, not to mention Mantanceros and what surely must have transpired there. These stories, sadly remain untold and their characters are summarilly dismissed. I do so wish I could have gotten to know them and the events that occurred while the Cassandra was at sea.<br /> That folks would have been a truly great book! Such remains our loss. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_69298004" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69298004" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69298004?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=pirates">pirates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69298004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13971795795477498722">First off, I have to say this is only my second Crichton novel. I read Jurassic Park back when the movie came out but haven't felt like reading anything else by him since. That being said, I enjoyed Pirate Latitudes. The novel does have its shortcomings but you have to wonder if this is because it wasn't truly finished. It's hard to say. This book was found on Crichton's computer after his death so it's possible that this wasn't the intended finished product. I liked it though and I'm curious to</span>
  <span id="freeText13971795795477498722" style="display:none">First off, I have to say this is only my second Crichton novel. I read Jurassic Park back when the movie came out but haven't felt like reading anything else by him since. That being said, I enjoyed Pirate Latitudes. The novel does have its shortcomings but you have to wonder if this is because it wasn't truly finished. It's hard to say. This book was found on Crichton's computer after his death so it's possible that this wasn't the intended finished product. I liked it though and I'm curious to see how it's adapted for film, Spielberg grabbed up the rights before the book was even published!<br /><br />I think the main problem I had was the lack of character development. It was hard for me to keep track of all the different pirates, sorry, <i>privateers</i>, and I completely forgot who the final villain was, vaguely remember him from the beginning. There's a lot of gruesome parts to the book that I think most people would have trouble with, but honestly didn't bother me, I think I'm just twisted. But there were some really creative ways that people were killed!<br /><br />The story was pretty crazy and action-packed and it's one of those where you are on the edge of your seat wondering what's going to happen next or what else could possibly go wrong for Captain Hunter as his crew. It was a different type of novel than I normally read and it was a nice divergence for me. It also really makes me want to go back and try something else from Crichton.<br /><br />All and all, a good final effort. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13971795795477498722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268440617?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jay" href="/user/show/7530340-jay">Jay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268440617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3511717674488691602">First, did you know that Michael Crichton is dead?!? This is the first of two books published posthumously, the second being Micro. <br/><br/>I've read a little Michael Crichton in the past - Sphere was wondeful, Prey was OK, Timeline was intriguing but ultimately corny. I have no idea what lead me to pick up Pirate Lattitudes, but it was fun. It is a strong entry in the Pirates versus Ninjas debate, and lends a much needed blow for the Pirates. <br/><br/>Set in the Carribean (primarily Jamaica) in the mid 1600's, </span>
  <span id="freeText3511717674488691602" style="display:none">First, did you know that Michael Crichton is dead?!? This is the first of two books published posthumously, the second being Micro. <br /><br />I've read a little Michael Crichton in the past - Sphere was wondeful, Prey was OK, Timeline was intriguing but ultimately corny. I have no idea what lead me to pick up Pirate Lattitudes, but it was fun. It is a strong entry in the Pirates versus Ninjas debate, and lends a much needed blow for the Pirates. <br /><br />Set in the Carribean (primarily Jamaica) in the mid 1600's, the protagonist is swashbuckling (I've used that word twice in two book reviews now) privateer Captain Hunter. At this point you may be asking yourself what the difference is between a pirate and a privateer. Turns out pirates are honest about their plundering, privateers do it under the guise of official cover. <br /><br />You know why I loved this book? Because I didn't have to think. There's no theme. There's no moral. There's nothing but a good old fashioned adventure story. Cannons. Swordfights. Explosions. Escapes. Huricanes. Hell, there's even a damsel in distress. In deference to his avowed profession as a novelist, Crichton obliges the reader with a nod towards a plot twist, though if it were a snowboard trick it would barely be a 180. Fast forward to the end: impossible mission completed, loot secured, damsel liberated (if you know what I mean), and bad guys dead. <br /><br />It's fun. Read it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3511717674488691602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78666164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78666164" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2884361-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339244733p2/2884361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78666164?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/2884361-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78666164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5798950631647485973">I had been looking forward to Pirate Latitudes ever since I'd learned of its existence. Michael Crichton knows (or knew, I suppose) how to craft an exciting novel. Crichton however peaked with Timeline, one of his best books, grounded in an historical setting. That's what I had been expeting to get with Pirate Latitudes. Unfortunately I was mistaken.<br/><br/>Pirate Latitudes is the story of Charles Hunter, privateer, and his crew of misfits as they attempt to take the Spanish galleon El Trinidad. The pre</span>
  <span id="freeText5798950631647485973" style="display:none">I had been looking forward to Pirate Latitudes ever since I'd learned of its existence. Michael Crichton knows (or knew, I suppose) how to craft an exciting novel. Crichton however peaked with Timeline, one of his best books, grounded in an historical setting. That's what I had been expeting to get with Pirate Latitudes. Unfortunately I was mistaken.<br /><br />Pirate Latitudes is the story of Charles Hunter, privateer, and his crew of misfits as they attempt to take the Spanish galleon El Trinidad. The premise is simple and lends itself to an exciting read. However, Hunter and his crew fall prey to one ridiculous plot point after another and by the novel's end all credulity has fled for safety. From a daring escape on an impregnable fortress to a hurricane to an attack from a kraken, Pirate Latitudes is an endless string of disasters.<br /><br />This novel can be summed up as The Italian Job circa 1665. It's heist novel meets Pirates of the Caribbean. In fact, this book could easily become the next 'Pirates' movie. While reading this novel I couldn't help but wonder if Crichton had any intention of publishing it had he lived, or at the very least if it wouldn't have undergone major revision first.<br /><br />An interesting premise with unfortunate execution. It's still worth a look if for nothing more than to see just how ridiculous things can get.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5798950631647485973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10631435569941136562" style="display:none">This was much different than the rest of Crichton's fiction that I've read. Those rely on theoretical science and well researched plots. <div id="review_1332243703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1332243703" />
    <a title="Rade " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8187431-rade"><img alt="Rade " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426096920p2/8187431.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1332243703?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rade " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rade " href="/user/show/8187431-rade">Rade </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1332243703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15429592584421250199">3.5<br/><br/>One thing I don't like is overly happy endings. If you got a story where the main characters go through what can only be described as a shitstorm, don't make them come out as heroes in every way possible. It is not practical and I hate it. Not saying this book was <i>exactly</i> like that but some points can be taken from my claim above. <br/><br/>This is one of those books that is hard to judge. On one hand you got a pirate story written by Crichton that was at times slow moving, but eventually it turned int</span>
  <span id="freeText15429592584421250199" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />One thing I don't like is overly happy endings. If you got a story where the main characters go through what can only be described as a shitstorm, don't make them come out as heroes in every way possible. It is not practical and I hate it. Not saying this book was <i>exactly</i> like that but some points can be taken from my claim above. <br /><br />This is one of those books that is hard to judge. On one hand you got a pirate story written by Crichton that was at times slow moving, but eventually it turned into a fun adventure story. On the other hand, you got a story about pirates and not enough blood spilled to satisfy my little crazy mind. I see pirates as crazy barbarians who raid ships, kill everyone on them, and escape with booty. Perhaps not all pirates (historically) were like that but I like to assume they were. <br /><br />That being said, I felt like something was missing in this book. Can't quite say what, but <i>something</i>. Maybe the pirates were not menacing enough, maybe there was not enough rioting, maybe there was not enough gold fondling, and maybe stop making it so the main characters are not so victorious in every way. One of the biggest reasons why I admire George R.R Martin is because he does not give a shit if you are attached to his character. he kills them in the next chapter without giving one solitary f*ck. Perhaps more authors should follow this route. <br /><br />With all that being said, the book was not bad. Sure, some parts were a bit awkward and forced while others were leaning a bit too far on the main characters side. Sometimes I read a passage and things happened exactly the way I predicted them. That is bad. I need surprises, the bigger the better. Other times I kept asking myself, "so after all the crap the characters have been through, you're telling me they still act as functional beings instead of pain struck sacks of meat?". Still, I had fun reading it and at 312 pages, I would not have been too mad even if the book was godawful. Crichton, like King, has good and bad books. This one was one a good, but not great scale. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15429592584421250199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2481860104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_99915845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99915845" />
    <a title="Rick Spilman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1865168-rick-spilman"><img alt="Rick Spilman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1272748914p2/1865168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99915845?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Spilman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Spilman" href="/user/show/1865168-rick-spilman">Rick Spilman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99915845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7594075679902647524">Pirate Latitudes by Micheal Crichton, published a year after his death, is a romp. It is full of swashbuckling action and completely familiar characters. There is a bold captain, who is either a privateer or a pirate; several fair and comely maidens of high birth and low; and a band of adventurers each with special skills and powers.<br/><br/>The rough and tumble hero, Captain Charles Hunter, sets off to capture a Spanish galleon laden with treasure, at anchor under the guns of an impregnable fortress.<br/><br/>He </span>
  <span id="freeText7594075679902647524" style="display:none">Pirate Latitudes by Micheal Crichton, published a year after his death, is a romp. It is full of swashbuckling action and completely familiar characters. There is a bold captain, who is either a privateer or a pirate; several fair and comely maidens of high birth and low; and a band of adventurers each with special skills and powers.<br /><br />The rough and tumble hero, Captain Charles Hunter, sets off to capture a Spanish galleon laden with treasure, at anchor under the guns of an impregnable fortress.<br /><br />He recruits for the mission a French assassin, named appropriately Sanson; a huge mute black man named Bassa but called the Moor; a powder and explosives expert, Don Diego, known either as Black Eye, or the Jew; and a woman, Lazue, who lives and dresses as a man and who happens to have uniquely keen eyesight as well as built in advantage in a knife fight when she flashes her womanly breasts to confuse her opponent. Then there is Enders, a barber/surgeon who is also a skilled helmsman. Crichton insists on calling Enders “the sea artist” repeatedly, referring to his abilities at the helm which border apparently on the magical.<br /><br />They will do battle with the horribly villainous Captain Cazalla, the Spanish commander of the fortress and an accompanying warship. Along the way the group picks up Lady Sarah Almont, the niece of the English Governor of Jamaica, who Cazalla has previously captured and ravished. Lady Sarah also happens to be a vegetarian and a witch. And just so that every base is covered Crichton even includes a Kraken, the mythological sea beast which made an appearance in the last two Disney Pirates of the Caribbean movies and will soon be making an encore in the upcoming movie, Clash of the Titans.<br /><br />Crichton uses every trick and ploy to keep the plot moving. The band of privateers is captured, then escapes, succeeds in capturing the galleon and rescuing the Governor’s niece, only to be chased by a Spanish warship. There is a sea battle, a hurricane, brushes with cannibals and the Kraken, as well as betrayals, murder, lusty wenches and some sex.<br />Admirers of nautical fiction will either be amused or irritated by Crichton’s descriptions of ships and sailing. He is often merely vague, which is a safe approach. Otherwise he confuses reefing with furling. The treasure ship starts out as a nao and becomes a galleon. While described as tubby and slow, the galleon travels at speeds that would not displease a clipper ship captain. At one key point in the plot Captain Hunter has all the guns on the galleon moved to the same side so he can fire them all at once. How this would work without corresponding gun ports is not clear. But then really who cares about accuracy when you have a Kraken?<br /><br />What sort of novel is Pirate Latitudes? It is a pot boiler, pulp fiction, and a fine book for the beach. The characters are all from central casting and the plot is reminiscent of many other books and movies. When the villain rasps “my mistress shall dine on your testicles,” I wasn’t sure whether to laugh, groan or just put the book down and walk away. But I kept reading.<br /><br />Pirate Latitudes is not a good book, nor is it a terribly bad book, nor is it so bad that it is good. It is the sort of book that you pick at the airport, read quickly while on a long flight and don’t care if you accidentally leave it on the plane.<br /><br />A movie of the novel, to be directed by Steven Spielberg, is under development. Of course.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7594075679902647524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129589908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129589908" />
    <a title="Gerald" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75671-gerald"><img alt="Gerald" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554985601p2/75671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129589908?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gerald" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gerald" href="/user/show/75671-gerald">Gerald</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129589908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11876459110860516034">Particularly since The Great Train Robbery, I often thought that Michael Crichton plotted his books deliberately so the movie scripts "fell out" of them. That is, his early work seems more literary, more novelistic, less structured like a three-act screenplay. Without any particular evidence except the usual Hollywood paranoia, I blamed his agents at CAA for insisting that he craft his novels with movie sales in mind. Obviously, given the path his career took, he succeeded spectacularly, at leas</span>
  <span id="freeText11876459110860516034" style="display:none">Particularly since The Great Train Robbery, I often thought that Michael Crichton plotted his books deliberately so the movie scripts "fell out" of them. That is, his early work seems more literary, more novelistic, less structured like a three-act screenplay. Without any particular evidence except the usual Hollywood paranoia, I blamed his agents at CAA for insisting that he craft his novels with movie sales in mind. Obviously, given the path his career took, he succeeded spectacularly, at least as a commercial phenomenon.<br /><br />But the richness of the narrative suffers. Not even tenth-grade reading level. Maybe seventh. Historically accurate, I suspect, but with the latter-day video-gamers' taste for gore layered on thick with a bloody trowel. Faces blown away from close pistol shot. Really? A Glock would perhaps do that job, but I think a pistol ball would leave a neat and disappointingly small hole.<br /><br />Then there's the first-act sequence of shots wherein the hero rounds up his accomplices for the mission. It's all there except for the music, which you can imagine from every other daring-voyage movie you ever saw.<br /><br />I thought the hero, pirate Captain Charles Hunter, was pretty much of a shit most of the time. But given the low-lifes he must hang with and the pervasive stink of injustice in his grimy, corrupt world, perhaps he can be forgiven. But he himself forgives not. Revenge is his, and don't let any little boy who aspires to grow up strong ever think it's wise or admirable or valiant to turn the other cheek. If you cross Hunter, he will smoke or cut or gut you. Count on it. And take your woman.<br /><br />I was even so cynical that I wondered whether this posthumous work was actually Crichton's, or just some ghostwritten pulp contracted for by CAA, with his name applied through the greedy concurrence of his heirs. Or maybe in the end he was mostly a master of Pulp Fiction.<br /><br />I was so curious, though, that I went to imdbpro.com to check on its possible status as a movie.<br /><br />"In Development" Steven Spielberg. The lamentably late Michael Crichton was set to direct.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11876459110860516034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2088297081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088297081" />
    <a title="Jonathan Maas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4837365-jonathan-maas"><img alt="Jonathan Maas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550771810p2/4837365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2088297081?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonathan Maas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonathan Maas" href="/user/show/4837365-jonathan-maas">Jonathan Maas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2088297081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7214871133706551370">A last testament to a brilliant author<br/><br/>They found this book on his hard drive, and lo and behold - it happens to be the best pirate book I've read. I had previously given that award to the incredible <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4558004.Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_The_Price_of_Freedom' title='Pirates of the Caribbean The Price of Freedom by A.C. Crispin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pirates of the Caribbean: The Price of Freedom</a>, but this has that Crichton-ness to it that just pushes it over the edge.<br/><br/>Brimming with authority, fun, going from one incredible scene to the next - I couldn't put this book down, and hung on every word.<br/><br/>Was Crichton a pirate author? No. But he put his ha</span>
  <span id="freeText7214871133706551370" style="display:none">A last testament to a brilliant author<br /><br />They found this book on his hard drive, and lo and behold - it happens to be the best pirate book I've read. I had previously given that award to the incredible <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4558004.Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_The_Price_of_Freedom" title="Pirates of the Caribbean The Price of Freedom by A.C. Crispin" rel="nofollow noopener">Pirates of the Caribbean: The Price of Freedom</a>, but this has that Crichton-ness to it that just pushes it over the edge.<br /><br />Brimming with authority, fun, going from one incredible scene to the next - I couldn't put this book down, and hung on every word.<br /><br />Was Crichton a pirate author? No. But he put his hat into the ring, and like so many times he's done that with a genre, he emerges a champion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7214871133706551370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127806171?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alins" href="/user/show/4244557-alins">Alins</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127806171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5520357196402888472"><br/>It's impossible to know whether Crichton intended this book to be published, or if he wrote it for fun. Considering it was written in 2006, and discovered on his hard drive after his death, it feels like maybe he wasn't rushing it off to his agent for publication.<br/><br/>It's not Crichton in peak form, that's for sure.<br/><br/>While the book is entertaining enough, it's missing what I love most about Crichton ... the research, the education, the intense build of excitement. It's a pirate story, and not a particu</span>
  <span id="freeText5520357196402888472" style="display:none"><br />It's impossible to know whether Crichton intended this book to be published, or if he wrote it for fun. Considering it was written in 2006, and discovered on his hard drive after his death, it feels like maybe he wasn't rushing it off to his agent for publication.<br /><br />It's not Crichton in peak form, that's for sure.<br /><br />While the book is entertaining enough, it's missing what I love most about Crichton ... the research, the education, the intense build of excitement. It's a pirate story, and not a particularly original one ... It's got your storms, your cannibals, your sea monsters, and general pirate treachery. The first half of the book I felt it was unforgivable that they decided to publish this. But the second half was fun enough that I can see it, and of course Spielberg is already working on the movie.<br /><br />I didn't love it, didn't hate it. I think, had Crichton been ready for publication it would have been better. Less flawed. But it was enjoyable enough, very fast paced and Amazon has a great deal on the hardcover so you almost can't go wrong.<br />Help other customers find the most helpful reviews <br />Was this review helpful to you? Yes No<br />	<br />	<br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_195960233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195960233" />
    <a title="Joseph Finley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5828919-joseph-finley"><img alt="Joseph Finley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515852295p2/5828919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195960233?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph Finley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph Finley" href="/user/show/5828919-joseph-finley">Joseph Finley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195960233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3995013358021137049">At barely 300 pages, Pirate Latitudes is a quick read that will remind Michael Crichton fans of The Great Train Robbery – except with pirates instead of Victorian-era thieves. <br/><br/>Set in 1665, Pirate Latitudes involves a team of privateers, each with unique talents, who are hired to capture a treasure-laden galleon from an island fortress ruled by a brutal Spanish commander. The novel’s protagonist is Captain Charles Hunter, a Harvard educated privateer from the Massachusetts Bay Colony, but it’s hi</span>
  <span id="freeText3995013358021137049" style="display:none">At barely 300 pages, Pirate Latitudes is a quick read that will remind Michael Crichton fans of The Great Train Robbery – except with pirates instead of Victorian-era thieves. <br /><br />Set in 1665, Pirate Latitudes involves a team of privateers, each with unique talents, who are hired to capture a treasure-laden galleon from an island fortress ruled by a brutal Spanish commander. The novel’s protagonist is Captain Charles Hunter, a Harvard educated privateer from the Massachusetts Bay Colony, but it’s his crew that makes the novel so enjoyable, including a Jewish explosives expert, a French assassin, a female marksman (who disguises herself as a man), and a mute strongman nicknamed The Moor. In addition to a seemingly impossible mission, there’s a thrilling battle at sea, a hurricane, and a twist at the end. This is not Crichton’s best novel, and I’m not even sure he was finished with it since the novel was discovered on his computer after his death. But I’m glad it was published. Pirate Latitudes is a thoroughly enjoyable read set during a fascinating period of history. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3995013358021137049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1853714935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1853714935" />
    <a title="Nigel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61463964-nigel"><img alt="Nigel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513313791p2/61463964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1853714935?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nigel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nigel" href="/user/show/61463964-nigel">Nigel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061929380" href="/book/show/6941923-pirate-latitudes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=17th-century">17th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61463964-nigel?shelf=nautical">nautical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1853714935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6886437092609692183">I quite liked this book, or at least the outline of the book that was published. You can definitely tell that this was an outline of a book, instead of an actual book. Although there are a couple of interesting characters, they are not really expanded on at all, and the story consists of one major action piece after another, without the usual level of detail devoted to each that you would expect. Also, there is a major plot development when the main character returns to Port Royal that is unexpe</span>
  <span id="freeText6886437092609692183" style="display:none">I quite liked this book, or at least the outline of the book that was published. You can definitely tell that this was an outline of a book, instead of an actual book. Although there are a couple of interesting characters, they are not really expanded on at all, and the story consists of one major action piece after another, without the usual level of detail devoted to each that you would expect. Also, there is a major plot development when the main character returns to Port Royal that is unexpected, and seems completely out of kilter with the character's involved - this definitely needed more work/back story.<br />Overall, the book reminded me quite a bit of Wilbur Smith - especially the Courtney novels set around the same time - quite a departure from the normal Michael Crichton fare, although he has written some adventure novels too (Timeline springs to mind). I think this would have been a much better book had Crichton been able to finish it properly, before he died (sad). I am not surprised they published it anyway though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6886437092609692183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157346186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1919392-adam-ross?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157346186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11331091102192003711">I've always been a Crichton fan, and just couldn't pass up the opportunity to read his take on pirates. This, Crichton's final book, was discovered among his affects after his untimely death in 2008, and HarperCollins published it essentially as they found it.<br/><br/>When a Spanish treasure galleon, separated from its convoy near Jamaica, is sighted taking refuge in the bay of the impenetrable Spanish fortress of Monteceros, the Governor of Port Royal commissions a ship of pirates to assault the fortres</span>
  <span id="freeText11331091102192003711" style="display:none">I've always been a Crichton fan, and just couldn't pass up the opportunity to read his take on pirates. This, Crichton's final book, was discovered among his affects after his untimely death in 2008, and HarperCollins published it essentially as they found it.<br /><br />When a Spanish treasure galleon, separated from its convoy near Jamaica, is sighted taking refuge in the bay of the impenetrable Spanish fortress of Monteceros, the Governor of Port Royal commissions a ship of pirates to assault the fortress and hijack the treasure ship. The novel follows the adventures of the most wanted pirate on the Spanish Main, Captain Charles Hunter and his crew, in their desperate attempt to take Monteceros and the treasure, and the increasingly difficult task of returning the treasure without running afoul the Spanish warships or the sadistic commander of Monteceros, Cazilla.<br /><br />With such a premise, you'd think it would have been a better book. I enjoyed it thoroughly, but as an aspiring writer, I can tell an early draft from a full-fleshed story. I see them all the time. And it seems that Crichton hadn't gone back and fleshed it out. It works as it stands, but it lacks that tense, Crichton flare, and exciting action (like trying to scale a four-hundred foot sheer cliff in a full gale) can get summarized instead of expanded to make it genuinely gripping. On the other hand, there are other scenes that read fine. Perhaps Crichton had rewritten them before his death. Either way, the bottom line; I liked it, but not Crichton's best.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11331091102192003711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_384123217" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384123217" />
    <a title="Robert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10374099-robert"><img alt="Robert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340263451p2/10374099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384123217?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert" href="/user/show/10374099-robert">Robert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384123217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6953354936470329170">Published posthumously, <i>Pirate Latitudes</i> was discovered as a complete manuscript on Crichton's computer after his death. For years Crichton had alluded to a project about Jamaica and the Caribbean, and from all indications, <i>Pirate Latitudes</i> is that project. Over the years I have developed a great interest in pirates, particularly the pirates of the Spanish Main---the old Caribbean of the 17th century. <i>Pirate Latitudes</i>is a rousing pirate tale based on a composite of historical characters Crichton</span>
  <span id="freeText6953354936470329170" style="display:none">Published posthumously, <i>Pirate Latitudes</i> was discovered as a complete manuscript on Crichton's computer after his death. For years Crichton had alluded to a project about Jamaica and the Caribbean, and from all indications, <i>Pirate Latitudes</i> is that project. Over the years I have developed a great interest in pirates, particularly the pirates of the Spanish Main---the old Caribbean of the 17th century. <i>Pirate Latitudes</i>is a rousing pirate tale based on a composite of historical characters Crichton researched. Like all of the author's novels, <i>Pirate Latitudes</i> is a page turner and moves at a break neck pace. Beyond the plot itself, which contains all the elements of a great adventure story, the novel features amazing nuggets of information regarding maritime practices of the period,anthropology,and British/Spanish colonial history, that sets Crichton above other best-selling authors of his genre. I truly loved this book and wished it was a series that went on forever. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6953354936470329170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2009162399" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9253445851517198094">I just remembered I read this during a trip to Ocho Rios several years ago. I believe it directly influenced how much I drank. With this book, you too can destroy your liver in attempt to escape lackluster prose, shitty characterization, and a story line that would make Ed Wood shake his head in weary disgust. <br/><br/>Do not do this to yourself. Pick up Powers's <i>On Stranger Tides</i>, Talty's <i>Empire of Blue Water</i>, or Cordingly's <i>Under the Black Flag</i> instead. </span>

<div id="review_3337923173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3337923173" />
    <a title="Michael Adamchuk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53614356-michael-adamchuk"><img alt="Michael Adamchuk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457705514p2/53614356.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3337923173?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Adamchuk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Adamchuk" href="/user/show/53614356-michael-adamchuk">Michael Adamchuk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53614356-michael-adamchuk?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53614356-michael-adamchuk?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53614356-michael-adamchuk?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53614356-michael-adamchuk?shelf=crichton-michael">crichton-michael</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53614356-michael-adamchuk?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3337923173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8677137530553680392">I really enjoyed this adventurous tale of pirates in the Caribbean in 1665. The manuscript was discovered, completed, after his death. Privateer Capt. Hunter (shades of Captain Jack Sparrow), with the financial support and blessing of Sir James Almont, governor of Jamaica, gathers a crew of characters Whisper, the Jew, Mr. Enders, The Moor, Lazue (a female posing as a male) and about 70 others. The objective is to capture a Spanish treasure galleon, the 'Trinidad', currently in the Spanish contr</span>
  <span id="freeText8677137530553680392" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this adventurous tale of pirates in the Caribbean in 1665. The manuscript was discovered, completed, after his death. Privateer Capt. Hunter (shades of Captain Jack Sparrow), with the financial support and blessing of Sir James Almont, governor of Jamaica, gathers a crew of characters Whisper, the Jew, Mr. Enders, The Moor, Lazue (a female posing as a male) and about 70 others. The objective is to capture a Spanish treasure galleon, the 'Trinidad', currently in the Spanish controlled harbor of Matanceros. On the way, Hunter's crew is captured by the feared Cazella. They manage a violent escape. They conduct a successful raid and capture the 'Trinidad'. During the escape, they are chased by a Spanish warship. They wage a serious sea battle and successfully escape only to run into a hurricane and then a "kraken" - a giant squid. Finally returning to Port Royal where the entire crew is taken into custody. Hunter is tried and convicted of being a pirate and sentenced to hang. In his absence, Sir James's secretary Mr. Hazlett and the commanding military officer, Scott have waged a coup and have Sir James locked up. His resident "housekeeper", Anne Sharpe abets Hunter's escape and he releases his other crew members. Hunter goes on a killing spree. In the epilogue, Crichton describes what happened to the remaining crew members and main characters. A fun filled, read with sex, violence and daring exploits.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8677137530553680392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gJwDYLYDCYxi0Y5sEM8NYUtlF2neZ0p7g4xCTTdqVN0GEepMxuHgCDfWnjgPXky+4R3RK/4pbgffWCS23zw8HA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C08H4uoLCP+OKlKZyashIqf1pB/m2otmTcs1xRKaJQaNwu7Omunhe9stQs3WOmD9DY1iXcaUrxoRH1M++sxNxw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">About Michael Crichton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1359042651p3/5194.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
13,857
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12435463878101166575">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On' title='Odds On' rel='nofollow noopener'>Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange' title='John Lange' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas' title='Michael Douglas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Michael Doug</a></span>
  <span id="freeText12435463878101166575" style="display:none">Michael Crichton (1942-2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On" title="Odds On" rel="nofollow noopener">Odds On</a>
</i> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange" title="John Lange" rel="nofollow noopener">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas" title="Michael Douglas" rel="nofollow noopener">Michael Douglas</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/607284.Jeffery_Hudson" title="Jeffery Hudson" rel="nofollow noopener">Jeffery Hudson</a>. His novel <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7663.A_Case_of_Need" title="A Case of Need" rel="nofollow noopener">A Case of Need</a>
</i> won the Edgar Award in 1969. Popular throughout the world, he has sold more than 200 million books. His novels have been translated into thirty-eight languages, and thirteen have been made into films.<br /><br />Michael Crichton passed away from lymphoma in 2008. He was 66 years old.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12435463878101166575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
